###Chapter 1 Shattered Promises

"Austin, don't."
Ella Brooks held her hands protectively across her chest, looking at the man hovering over her. She hadn't expected Austin Raymond to return home after two months of tabloid scandals, much less for him to immediately seek such sudden and overwhelming intimacy.
The bedroom was dimly lit, with only a small bedside lamp casting a warm yellow glow that highlighted Austin's chiseled features and sharp profile. His piercing eyes reminded her of a hawk—predatory and intense. Without many words, his presence enveloped her, his movements carrying a cold determination, as if he were fulfilling a predetermined objective rather than seeking a connection.
Despite her reservations, a surge of familiar longing welled up within Ella. As the rain began to patter against the windows, a silent, bittersweet passion unfolded between them—a dance of shadows and suppressed emotions. Outside, the thunder rolled, creating a natural melody with the heavy atmosphere inside the room.
When the night finally settled into a heavy silence, Ella felt utterly drained, her spirit feeling as if it had been weathered by a storm. She watched Austin as he stood by the window, already distant, the warmth of their encounter vanishing like mist.
His low, husky voice finally broke the quiet. "Ella, we need a child."
The words weren't a plea, but a cold declaration tinged with the bitterness of an unspoken bargain. In that instant, clarity flickered in Ella’s eyes, while an overwhelming bitterness settled deep within her heart.
Indeed. Judith was returning. He didn't want a family with her; he required an heir to fortify his standing, to appease his grandmother, and to clear the obstacles for the woman he truly loved. A wry sense of self-deprecation flickered in her mind; this time, Austin would surely be disappointed, as her body had long been fragile and ill-suited for such a task.
"Is that understood?" Austin’s voice carried a hardness born from a need for control.
Summoning every ounce of her strength, Ella suppressed the bone-deep chill. "Yes," she whispered through clenched teeth.
Later, as she emerged from the bathroom wrapped in a robe, she heard Austin speaking on the phone with a tenderness he never showed her. "Don't be afraid. Wait for me at home, I'll come right over."
Ella froze. She didn't need to guess who was on the other end. This gentle side of Austin was a sanctuary reserved only for Judith. As Austin grabbed his coat and walked unhesitatingly into the rainy night, Ella realized she had never truly left that frozen mountain of her youth. The cold had stayed with her, and tonight, it finally reached her marrow.
The Raymond family had strict rules: as the eldest grandson, Austin must produce an heir to fully inherit the family fortune. If not for that legacy, he wouldn't be here.
"Remember to take your medicine," he instructed coldly before leaving. This time, it wasn't a precaution to prevent a life, but fertility medication to force one. Once he secured his inheritance, he could finally be rid of her.
As the tail lights of his Maybach disappeared into the rain, Ella collapsed onto the bed. Her mind drifted back to the past—to the ten-year-old Austin who promised to protect her, and the eighteen-year-old Austin who promised to marry her. She remembered the three years she spent by his side during his paralysis, helping him through the darkness when everyone else, including Judith, had abandoned him.
She had thought she could melt his icy heart. But Judith's return proved that a single glance from the other woman was enough to make her years of devotion vanish.
The next morning, the headlines confirmed her heartache: Austin had been seen entering Judith's home late at night. Amidst the media frenzy, a message arrived from him: [Wait for me at home tonight. Take your folic acid regularly.]
Ella looked at the screen, tears sliding down her face. To him, she was merely a tool—a vessel to free him from his obligations so he could finally fly to the woman he truly desired.
###Chapter 2 Grandmother's Awakening

A shrill ring pierced the silence of Ella's empty house.

When she answered, her face instantly paled. "What did you say?Grandmother collapsed? I'm coming right now!"


Ella rushed toward the door, not noticing the housekeeper's contemptuous glance as she left.


"Ella is on her way to the Raymond estate now," the housekeeper reported into her phone once Ella was gone.


From Ella's modern townhouse to the Raymond family estate in Golden Oak, the drive normally took thirty minutes.


Ella drove recklessly fast, her mind racing with worry.

Karen had always been in excellent health. What could have possibly caused her to collapse so suddenly?


When Ella finally arrived at the sprawling colonial mansion, she was led to Karen's bedroom, where she was unconscious on the bed.


Margaret Raymond, Austin's mother, stood nearby with an unmistakable look of displeasure.


Austin stood with his brow furrowed, his back to the door.

Ella noticed his shirt was torn, revealing glimpses of bloodied skin beneath.



The sight immediately gave her a clue about what had happened.

She hurried forward,concern evident in her voice. "What happened to Grandmother? Why did she collapse suddenly?"
Margaret turned to Ella, her accumulated anger seemingly findmg ns target. "Ella, what exactly did you tell your grandma? How dare you bring her to this state? Is being married into the Raymond family such a burden for you?"


Ella's eyes grew cold, a hint of mockery visible in their depths. "You know perfectly well that Grandmother's health is fragile. Yet you allowed those tabloid stories to circulate unchecked."


Since his marriage to Ella, Austin had been constantly surrounded by scandals involving Judith, which had filled the gossip columns.

Yesterday, when he rushed to be with Judith during the storm, it had apparently been the final straw for Karen.


Margaret's expression darkened further. "How dare you! If not for your calculated schemes, would you have married Austin? Everything you have now was stolen from Judith!"


She looked Ella up and down with undisguised contempt.

In the eyes of the Raymond family, only Judith was worthy of being Austin's wife.


Everything Ella had sacrificed and endured apparently counted for nothing.


A sharp pain stabbed through Ella's chest, making it difficult to breathe.


"You've taken what doesn't belong to you for long enough," Margaret continued. "When will you finally divorce Austin and return what rightfully belongs to Judith?"

Just as Ella was about to respond, Karen coughed weakly and began to stir.

Ella quickly moved to her side, concern flooding her voice. "Grandmother,
how are you feeling? Is anything hurting?"

Karen slowly shook her head.

Ella carefully positioned a pillow behind Karen's back to help her sit up.

"Grandmother." Austin said, his voice complex with emotion.

Karen's piercing gaze swept over Austin before settling on Margaret.

"Don't think that just because I'm old. I've become senile and blind to the underhanded tactics you're employing," Karen said sharply. "As long as T m alive. I remain in control of the Raymond family, and Ella remains the only granddaughter-in-law I recognize. Those vultures circling outside can keep dreaming."

A warmth spread through Ella's heart.

Since her marriage. Karen had been the only person who consistently stood by her side.

No matter what happened, she always supported Ella unfailingly.

In her prime, Karen had been as capable as any man, even saving the company from the brink of collapse during its most desperate hour.

Karen trusted her judgment of character.

When Judith had abandoned Austin at his lowest point,choosing to study abroad rather than stand by him, Karen had seen hertrue nature.

Such a woman didn't deserve Austin,regardless of how well she could manipulate him and Margaret with her charm and pretty words.

Margaret shifted uncomfortably under Karen's rebuke. "Mother,these two only married because of manipulation and circumstance.Continuing this farce benefits neither of them. They should free each other while they still
can."

Karen's gaze grew even sharper. "Even if they were to divorce-which I don't support-Judith would never be welcomed into this family! Besides.Ella was as much a victim in that situation as anyone."

This statement sent ripples through Ella's heart, bringing with it waves of bitter memories.

It was true that she had harbored feelings for Austin for years.

But her marriage to Austin had ultimately benefited the Raymond family more than herself.

Throughout their four years together, she had been branded as the manipulative gold-digger who trapped Austin.

The truth was that she had given everything she could tothis marriage,exhausting herself over fourteen years of unrequited love.

"Mother," Margaret began, unwilling to yield.

"Enough!" Karen's voice turned icy. "I will not hear another word defending Judith. Being a homewrecker and destroyingsomeone else's marriage hardly makes her a prize!"


Margaret was silenced, though her resentful glare at Ella spoke volumes.

If not for Austin's accident, Judith would never have lost her place beside him.


Karen then turned her attention to Austin. "And you don't forget who stood by your side when it mattered most!"

Austin's lips tightened into a thin line. "Grandmother, Judith explained everything to me. She was forced to go abroad back then. She had no
Karen laughed coldly. "And you actually believe that? You're the oniy one who would."

Austin's frown deepened. "Grandmother, you're misunderstanding Judith."

"I don't judge people by what they say," Karen retorted. "I judge them by what they do. And her actions speak volumes."

Ella sighed inwardly.

Karen reached out her hand, and Ella moved closer. She gripped Ella's hand firmly.

"My dear child, I know you've endured countless injustices these past years. As long as I'm here, I won't allow anyone to mistreat you."

Ella felt a sudden tightness in her throat.

Being bullied, ignored, and maliciously judged had become so commonplace that she had grown numb to it all.

But being shown genuine concern made her eyes sting with unexpected emotion.


Ella clenched her fist silently.

She knew how much Karen valued the continuation of the Raymond bloodline,but with her physical condition making conception difficult,she didn't want to disappoint the only person who truly supported her.


Before she could speak, Austin stepped forward, determination flashing in his eyes.

"Grandmother, the media has already uncovered Judith's identity. I must ensure her safety. This divorce has to happen!"
###Chapter 3 Unexpected News

Ella lifted her gaze. quietly meeting his eyes. Before her stood a man who,for the sake of another woman, dared to dlefy the most revered matriarch,shamelessly trampling upon Ella's dignity in front of the entire family.

In that moment, the tightly wound string within Ella's heart, strained for fourteen years, snapped with a sharp, irrevocable crack.

It was not the absence of pain, but pain so profound it numbed her entirely. Suddenly, exhaustion and bitter irony overcame her. After all these years of sacrifice, she could not even retain a shred of dignity before his grandmother.

So be it; it was time to end it.

Her voice was calm and undisturbed, imbued with a liberation even she had yet to recognize: "Grandma, I consent to the divorce."

Karen's disbelief was palpable as she fixed her gaze on Ella.

Austin abruptly turned his head, his eyes burning into her. Her composure left a hollow ache in his chest, as though something precious had been wrenched away instantaneously.

This alien sensation of losing control vexed him, and he hastily dismissed it as another one of her manipulative ploys.

What new scheme was she attempting? Playing the victim before his grandmother? The art of feigned retreat?

Karen regained her composure, clearing her throat. "What matters is that you have a child."
Ella looked at her with resignation. "Grandma, you must not know that when I was eighteen. I was trapped on a snowy mountain and severely harmed by the cold. The chances of me conceiving in this lifetime are infinitesimal."


The snowy mountain?

Austin's expression shifted subtly; this was the second time that word had slipped from her lips today, yet he had no recollection of it.

Instinctively, he wanted to question her further, but Ella had already turned away, refusing to meet his gaze. That detached demeanor only intensified the restlessness gnawing at his heart.

Margaret eagerly interjected, "The Raymond family empire needs an heir!Mother, no matter how much you like Ella, don't you need to think about the future? This divorce must happen."

Karen remained silent, her eyes fixed on Ella with a complex expression.

Ella gently squeezed Karen's hand and nodded reassuringly.

Right now, stabilizing Karen's condition was the priority.


Karen closed her eyes. When she opened them again, her expression had softened considerably.

"Ella, whatever decision you make, I'll support you."

She understood how deeply Ella loved Austin, which was why she wanted to give her a chance.

She had always pressured Austin, hoping he would treat Ella well and recognize her worth.
Ella looked at her with resignation. "Grandma, you must not know that when I was eighteen, I was trapped on a snowy mountain and severely harmed by the cold. The chances of me conceiving in this lifetime are infinitesimal."


The snowy mountain?

Austin's expression shifted subtly; this was the second time that word had slipped from her lips today, yet he had no recollection of it.

Instinctively, he wanted to question her further, but Ella had already turned away, refusing to meet his gaze. That detached demeanor only intensified the restlessness gnawing at his heart.

Margaret eagerly interjected, "The Raymond family empire needs an heir!Mother, no matter how much you like Ella, don't you need to think about the future? This divorce must happen."

Karen remained silent, her eyes fixed on Ella with a complex expression.

Ella gently squeezed Karen's hand and nodded reassuringly.

Right now, stabilizing Karen's condition was the priority.

Karen closed her eyes. When she opened them again, her expression had softened considerably.

"Ella, whatever decision you make.I'll support you."

She understood how deeply Ella loved Austin, which was why she wanted to give her a chance.


She had always pressured Austin, hoping he would treat Ella well and recognize her worth,
But reality had turned out vastly different from her expectations.

Ella had suffered countless wounds in this marriage. Perhaps this was simply an unfortunate fate.

Ella felt a warmth spread through her heart.

Austin's gaze grew increasingly intense.

If not for Karen's concern about continuing the family line, he wouldn't have considered staying with Ella for another minute.

Surely, this must be yet another of her cunning stratagems,an act of feigned misery designed to elicit sympathy before his grandmother.

The more she behaved this way, the more his aversion grew.

Ignoring Austin's watchful gaze. Ella spoke briefly with Karen,encouraging her to rest and takecare of herself before quickly leaving the mansion.


Standing outside, Ella tilted her head back to look at the sky.

There had been a time when she believed nothing could ever drive her and Austin to divorce.


Divorcing him felt like taking a knife and carving out the softest part of her heart.


Though the pain was excruciating and left her bleeding, she had no regrets.

Footsteps approached from behind.

Austin walked up to her, his eyes cold and dangerous.
"Ella, whatever scheme you're plotting, stop it now. Judith nearly had to be rushed to the emergency room last night. Drop your manipulative tactics. It only makes me despise you more!"

Judith had threatened suicide because of her, and he couldn't wait any longer. Even without his inheritance, he was determined to be with Judith.

"Did you really think I wanted to marry you for any reason other than having a child?"


Ella suddenly felt her chest constrict painfully.

All her previous efforts to be kind to Austin had been interpreted as ulterior motives.


Even her attempt to preserve their marriage for Karen's sake was being branded as despicable and underhanded!


In Austin's eyes, was she truly so monstrous, like some destructive force of nature?

"In all these four years, did you ever have even the slightest feeling for me?"She asked.


Austin's narrow eyes narrowed slightly, imbued with disdain and malice,as if indulging in the absurdity of the grandest jest.

In that moment. his silence provided the answer.

He spoke coldly, "If you agree to divorce. I'll meet any demands you have,including the deed to this townhouse."


There wasn't a shred of affection.

Was there truly nothing between them at all?
Ella shook her head in despair. "I don't need your compensation."


To Austin, it was clear that she didn't want any connection with him,nor did she want him to feel guilty over their failed marriage.

Could money really buy out her marriage?

What did she really mean to Austin?

But her reaction registered differently to Austin.

To him, Ella clearly thought the offer was insufficient; she wanted more.

He was convinced he had judged her correctly: a selfish, vicious, and endlessly greedy woman.

"Ella, what exactly do you want?" Austin's tone was tinged with contempt.

Fighting back tears, Ella replied, "Austin, I'll give you what you want."

Yet Austin showed no happiness at hearing the words he had sought for so long.

Instead,he felt an inexplicable unease about finally being free of Ella.

It was as though he was about to lose someone vital to him.

No, that couldn't be right; this must be another of her tricks.

"Hopefully, that is the case." He revealed nothing but disdain,muttering that they would sign the divorce papers and file at court in a few days before storming off.

After composing herself. Ella took out her phone to call her best friend.

As the call connected, her vision suddenly darkened as overwhelming
blackness engulfed her.

When Ella regained consciousness,she found herself in a ward.

She looked at the IV drip in her arm, trying to recall her last moments before fainting.


What had happened? Why had she collapsed so suddenly?

Her friend Sarah Wilson entered from outside, visibly relieved to see Ella awake.


"Ella, you're finally conscious. Do you have any idea how terrified I was?You called me, but didn't say anything before the line went dead. I rushed over immediately. Thank goodness I arrived in time to get you to the hospital."


Ella's voice was raspy. "Thankyou, Sarah. But did the doctor say why I fainted so suddenly?"

Her health had always been good.

This shouldn't have happened.

Sarah gestured toward the door. "Not yet. Let's wait for the doctor to explain."

As she finished speaking, the doctor entered, reviewing the test results in his hands.


"Ms. Brooks, congratulations. You're one and a half months pregnant!"

Ella's pupils constricted in disbelief.

She even suspected she had misheard, yet her voice betrayed her
excitement.

"I'm pregnant?"

Ella couldn't hide the smile spreading across her face.

She had been hoping for this child for a very long time.

Now her wish had finally come true.
###Chapter 4 Bittersweet News

Pregnant? Just as she resolved to completely relinquish Austin,to abandon their marriage, the child arrived.

This was not a continuation of their entanglement, but a rebirth belonging solely to Ella. She gently placed her hand on her abdomen, her eyes shining for the first time with a light that had nothing to do with Austin.

"Baby, from now on, it's just you and me." She no longer needed him; she would forge a new world for herself and her child.


"Doctor, what should Ella be aware of regarding her current condition?"Sarah asked, standing beside the hospital bed after recovering from her initial shock.


Ella immediately jumped in with her own question. "Can I be discharged?"

The doctor's expression turned serious as he glanced at the medical report in his hand.


He answered Ella first, then instructed Sarah. "There aren't ainy major issues preventing discharge, but her physical condition is extremely poor.She needs proper rest. There's a significant risk of miscarriage at any time."

Sarah nodded, accepting the responsibility.

After the doctor left, Sarah helped Ella with the discharge paperwork.


As they exited the ward, Sarah supported Ella, her eyes filled with concern."Are you sure you don't want to stay in the hospital a few more days?"

"No. I can't stand being cooped up in that room. The antiseptic smell is suffocating."
Sarah continued supporting Ella as they walked, her face etched with worry. "Does Austin know you're pregnant?"

She had heard how Austin had pressured Ella relentlessly about getting pregnant.

As Ella's friend, she couldn't help but feel protective.

Yet when Ella married Austin, there was little she could do.

"You were right, Sarah. Austin and I were never right for each other," Ella said.


The advice Sarah had given her years ago, which Ella had dismissed,now felt painfully prophetic after experiencing the harsh reality firsthand.

She finally understood how naive she had been.

Sarah stopped walking, looking at her friend with concern."Ella?"

After taking a deep breath, Ella looked at her with tear-filled eyes. "I'm filing for divorce."

Sarah froze, her eyes widening in disbelief. "Divorce? Did Austin hurt you again?"

Ella remained silent.

"You know what I'm feeling right now? It's like following a book to what you think is going to be a happy ending, only to discover the author completely ruined the final Chapter. I always thought that even if you weren't in love; you and Austin would at least have a comfortable life together."

Sarah's heart ached as she looked at Ella's thin frame, seething with rage.
"Let me confront him and set things straight!"'Sarah said.

Ella grabbed her hand and shook her head. "I don't want to drag you into this complicated situation."

Sarah's gaze was fraught with complexity. "Ella, have you truly made up your mind?"


Ella nodded firmly, her gaze unwavering.

"All right, whatever you decide, I'm behind you one hundred percent."

Sarah's immediate support warmed Ella's heart.

Having such a loyal friend was truly a blessing.

As evening fell, darkness descended, and a bright moon hung in the sky.

Ella entered the security code-0623-to unlock the mansion door.

Austin had never changed the code, always using these four digits.

She had often wondered about the significance of this number, but whenever she asked Austin, he never gave her a straight answer.

She hesitated before pushing the door open, finding the interior empty,

Moonlight streamed through the floor-to-ceiling windows,casting shadowy tree silhouettes across the floor.

Had Austin not returned home?

The household staff was also absent.

Looking around, she decided not to linger.
She had come to collect her belongings.

Since she had decided on separation, she wanted a clean break.


Ella opened the wardrobe and immediately caught sight of two neatly segregated rows of clothing.


The crispness of the suits intermingled with the delicate elegance of the skirts, creating a strangely comforting tableau.

For a fleeting moment, Ella was caught off guard.


Although the household chores were predominantly entrusted to the maid.Ella always took it upon herself to organize the clothes,believing that this intimate act nurtured the essence of their marriage.


Yet, in the end, it was merely self-deception.

Drawing a deep breath, she cast aside the thought,hastily gathered her clothes, and packed a few essentials before placing the prepared divorce agreement on the bedside table.

If she was intent on leaving, she resolved to do so decisively.

Having completed these tasks, Ella summoned a moment by the villa's entrance to dial Austin's number.


Before he could utter a word, she straightforwardly announced,

"The divorce agreement is on the bedside table. Remember to sign it."


What followed was a long silence,punctuated only by the crackling static of the phone line, a silence so prolonged it feIt like an eternity.

Just as Ella almost presumed he had hung up, a voice, softer and far more
gentle than before, finally came through the receiver.


"You went to the hospital?"

Ella froze.

He rarely showed concern for her. Why would he suddenly ask about this?

She didn't answer his question, instead pressing on. "Austin. I'm trying to discuss something important."

"You need to take better care of yourself. I've given you so many supplements, yet you're still this frail."

Austin continued, speaking as if to himself.

Ella furrowed her brow, a trace of irritation flickering across her features.In the next moment, she understood the reason behind Austin's sudden change of heart.


"There is a banquet. You are required to attend as my companion." His voice issued forth, cold and commanding.


It was no longer a husband consulting his wife, but a superior issuing orders to a subordinate.


Perhaps, in this fragile dynamic, Austin had grown accustomed to her countless capitulations, assuming she lacked the resolve to refuse.


Clutching the phone tightly, Ella instinctively wished to decline.

"I have work to attend to," He said.

Without hesitation, he cut her off and mercilessly ended the call.
A suffocating wave washed over her, rendering her hands limp at her sides.



What, in this marriage, was she truly? A wife? A mere companion for carnal indulgence? Or merely an obedient marionette. bound to obey?

In the end. Ella resolved to acquiesce.

She left her luggage at Sarah's residence, quickly composed herself.and set off toward the banquet.


As her high heels clicked against the marble floor. Ella noticed Austin in the center of the lavish hotel, holding a glass of red wine. engaged in conversation.

Just as she was about to approach him, a graceful, petite figure blocked her view, linking arms with Austin in a gesture of extreme intimacy,her face radiant with joy.


Ella halted, her expression stiffening.

It was Judith.
###Chapter 5 Overshadowed

Judith's lavish and elegant light purple mermaid gown with its cinched waist highlighted her slender figure. The sequins on the skirt shimmered like fish scales under the chandelier lights, making her the undeniable focal point of the evening.

She looked like a unique masterpiece amid the sea of guests.

Every eye in the ballroom was fixed on Judith.

Austin,by her side, was no exception; his gaze never wavered from her.imbued with boundless tenderness.

Coupled with the recent scandal that had stirred quite the tumult, those around them could not help but speculate about the nature of their relationship.

Ella lowered her eyelids, a faint, icy smile curling upon her slender lips.

Did Austin summon her to this banquet merely to flaunt their affection for Judith?


If so,it was utterly unnecessary.

She sneered inwardly, enduring the surrounding accolades lauding their beauty as a couple, unwilling to stoop to such humiliation.

Yet, fate seemed determined to deny her such solace. No sooner had she turned than a feigned voice of surprise rose behind her.

"Ella? What a coincidence! You're here too?"

Ella froze in her steps, her spine stiffening, an indescribable wave of
revulsion washing over her.

Like a nightingale, the melodic, soft voice oozed false sweetness designed to charm.


Ella turned to face them, her countenance unreadable.

Yet Judith seemed oblivious to her rejection, stepping closer with affectionate familiarity, a faint blush tinting her cheeks.

"Were you looking for Austin? He went to the restroom, and you had no idea. Several people even mistook me for his wife. It was so awkward."

Judith covered her face with her hand, feigning shyness while her eyes sparkled with unmistakable provocation.

Unmoved, Ella's face remained impassive as she replied coolly.

"Oh, that must have been quite embarrassing."

Taken aback by her serene response. Judith nearly faltered in her performance.

Feigning innocence, she peered at Ella and asked.

"Ella, are you upset? I didn't mean to take your place. If it bothers you.I can explain to them."


As she spoke. Judith abruptly grasped Ella's hand.

Automatically. Ella withdrew, frowning as shestepped back. "No need."

Her resolute demeanor exhausted whatever patience Judith had left.

Her gaze flicked around before settling into a cold expression.eyes flashing
with arrogance and disdain. "What are you pretending to? Clinging to the title of Mrs. Raymond for so long, you really think you're the legitimate wife Austin chose to marry? You know better than anyone how you schemed to stay by his side. If you don't want to embarrass yourself, you'd better behave and stop clinging to him."

Watching her twisted and snarling face, a thought suddenly struck Ella's mind.


Could it be that Austin had yet to inform her that they were already preparing for divorce?

Feeling vexed, her tone sharpened, "When it comes to scheming. I certainly don't compare to you. Tell me, if Austin learned you weren't truly coerced back then, do you think he wouldn't turn against you?"

Judith's expression darkened as sheglared fiercely. "If you dare spread lies,
I won't let you off!"

"You're welcome to try."

Since divorce was imminent anyway, Ella said no more and brushed past Judith in search of Austin.


Originally, she had no intention of confronting Austin about this, but Judith's earlier conduct had ignited her ire.

It took little effort to spot Austin smoking alone in the corridor.

His solitary figure stood desolate in the empty passageway,silhouetted against the window.


Two slender fingers pinched the cigarette, wisps of blue smoke curling forth from beneath his aquiline nose. In that moment, his austere features
seemed infused with a rare allure, the flickering embers in his hand castinga subtle,restless glow.


This was the first time Ella had seen Austin smoke.

It brought back memories.

At twenty-five, confined to a wheelchair. Austin had grown gloomy and taciturn.


Whenever Ella tried to get close, he would push her away with harsh words.


But Ella hadn't taken it personally. She'd been willing to give Austin time to emerge from his darkness.


One day after they'd argued, Ella had noticed the smell of cigarettes on his suit.


She'd assumed it came from a business dinner and hadn't questioned it.

Later,she learned that a business partner had withheld funds and verbally attacked Austin at a meeting, calling him a cripple who couldn't even stand.


The insults had been vicious.

Furious, Ella had confronted the man at his office building, gotten into a physical altercation, and ended up at the police station.

How much she had loved him then. How ridiculous it seemed now.

Ella's self-mocking laugh caught Austin's attention.

His eyes registered surprise before he methodically extinguished his
cigarette and regarded her. "You're here."

"Why is Judith here?" She demanded.

Ella felt as though, in his eyes, she was naught but a fool, summoned at will and dismissed without a second thought.

Tears welled fiercely within her eyelids, and her chest seemed flooded with a tide of salty bitterness; she was utterly disheartened.

All along, it appeared she had merely demeaned herself with false humility.



"If you no longer require me, then I shall be taking my leave."

Without another word, Ella turned and strode away.

Behind her, Austin's expression darkened as he abruptly reached out and grasped her wrist. "Ella, don't be unreasonable!”

Frowning deeply, Austin saw no fault in himself and spoke with growing impatience.


She shrugged off his hand, restraining her emotions to prevent an outburst."Since you've already found another companion, what purpose do I serve by staying here?"

His grip tightened on her wrist, voice dropping to a low warning. "Ella,provoking me will do you no favors!"

Scoffing coldly, she struggled to wrench her hand free. "That's a warning I should be giving you!"


Fury coursed through her veins, blinding her to her surroundings.
Suddenly, a glass of red wine was hurled from beside her, spilling entirely across her garments.

Her brow furrowed sharply as she turned to find Judith standing there.face flushed with shock and helpless apology. "Sorry, I didn't do it on purpose."
###Chapter 6 The Wine Stain

"I'm sorry." Judith stumbled back repeatedly, her face etched with terror.

Ella could never forget the fleeting look of provocation that had crossed her face moments before; she knew it was all a facade.

All around them, countless eyes turned in their direction, unwavering and piercing. Whispers began to ripple through the crowd. weaving a tapestry of murmured speculation around the two women.

"Did you see her with Mr. Raymond? I bet she's trying to seduce him." A woman whispered.

"Ms. Brooks should dump a glass of red wine on her. Teach her a lesson."another added.


"Why is Ms. Brooks being so nice? She shouldn't have apologized to her at all."


Ella heard the venomous comments directed at her.

Every cruel word landed like a slap.

The ironywas suffocating. Judith had deliberately spilt wine on her dress.yet somehow Ella had become the villain in everyone's eyes.


Seething with fury, Ella glanced down at the glaring crimson stain marring her gilded gown, her fingers tightening subtly.


Before she could utter a word, Judith preempted her, assuming a pitiful demeanor as if wronged. "Austin, you must explain to Ella; please tell her not to be angry with me!"
She gently tugged at Austin's sleeve, casting a timid glance at Ella.

Her father. John Brooks, burdened by her mother's death,brought along his mistress, Carol Baker, and Judith, two years older, establishing a legitimate marriage.

Her grandmother suffered a stroke from the shock and never recovered.

Her husband was entwined with her half-sister in a seemingly perfect union.

She never revealed her true origin; thus, everyone sought to trample her beneath their feet.

What? Limited edition?
###Chapter 7 Fire and Betrayal

She tried to move away but discovered she had twisted her ankle.

From a distance,she could see Judith coldly watching the scene unfold.

Until a figure emerged from the flames.
###Chapter 8 Betrayal and Loss

He gradually walked toward them through the smoke.

He had truly abandoned her.

Pain sliced through her nerves, yet her heart felt strangely numb.

In the endless sea of flames, she was like an abandoned sailboat, utterly alone.

Some showed laughter, while others revealed her sitting alone at a fully se dinner table.

This must be a nightmare.

The devastating news hit Ella like a thunderbolt, leaving her trembling uncontrollably.


It wasn't a dream.

The baby she had struggled so hard to conceive was gone.

She refused to believe it. These people had to be lying.

They were wrapped in multiple layers of bandages.

You lost a considerable amount of blood from your lower body,so the attending physician took conservative measures to prevent nerve damage and potential paralysis-removing the glass fragments before stopping the bleeding."

Her baby should have been safe.

Her legs were injured, but the baby shouldn't have been affected.

How could they not have saved her child?

Something had gone wrong in the procedure.

no choice but to..."

"Enough. Since this matter has been clarified, there's no need to make a fuss."
###Chapter 11 The Breaking Point

###Chapter 13 The Painful Truth

Her baby.

###Chapter 14 Come Back

###Chapter 15 Broken Pieces

###Chapter 16 Start Over

For the past four years. Ella had put her career on hold for her family.

She'd once been brilliant, renowned as "Phoenix" in academic circles,pioneering groundbreaking research in autonomous vehicles and advanced Al systems.

But that was before she'd skipped ahead in her education to follow Austin's footsteps into prestigious institutions.

She had been like someone blinded by love, chasing desperately after Austin.


Even knowing that Austin and Judith were considered the perfect couple by everyone around them.


She had never given up.

So when she received acceptance letters from internationally recognized institutions, she chose to decline.


Multiple companies had extended job offers, hoping she would join them immediately upon graduation.


Quantum Tech had been among them.

But she had been too foolish, too blinded, with Austin occupying her every thought.

Perhaps God had taken pity on her determination.

Right when everything seemed hopeless, Austin had his accident.

After he became paralyzed, she stayed by his side day and night, caring for
him tirelessly, repeatedly hoping for a miracle, praying he would stand again.


To treat his paralysis, she even returned to studying medicine and giving lectures at various universities, creating treatment plans, all in the hope of finding that one-in-a-hundred chance that might help Austin walk again.


Her persistence paid off; her efforts succeeded.

Yet somehow. Judith reaped the benefits of her hard work.

She had come so close.

When it came to pursuing Austin, she seemed perpetually clueless.

Why was that?


It was more difficult to decode than any research problem, as if some cosmic force had predetermined that they could never be together.

The night before her interview, Ella pulled a dust-laden trunk from beneath the bed. Upon opening it, she found an aged yet meticulously maintained laptop and several trophies.

She powered on the device; the screen illuminated to reveal a desktop adorned with the codename "Phoenix."


Within the folders lay documents detailing her participation in various prestigious national scientific research competitions during her university years,alongside an unfinished project model entitled "Optimization of Perception Fusion Algorithms for Autonomous Driving."


Gently tracing the codename on the screen, she whispered, "Ella, welcome back."
The gentle breeze caressed her face as Ella entered the building.

Quantum Tech stood as the most representative company in the scientific research community. Their advanced AI products had dramatically increased the company's market value and influence upon release.Subsequently, they became the industry leader in autonomous vehicles.

They had shocked the world twice.

These achievements had cemented Quantum Tech's position in the scientific research community.

A handful of people moved through the spacious lobby. Ella made her way through them toward the reception desk.

"Here for the interview? Follow me."

She was about to head for the elevator when a soft vroice asked from behind her.


"Excuse me, which floor is the interview on?"

She was here for an interview, too.

Ella's expression remained unchanged as she quickly averted her gaze.
This had nothing to do with her.

Ella didn't answer.

"Isn't that too much trouble?" Judith asked with a shy smile.

"Don't go out of your way. I just wanted to try this out," Judith replied modestly.

The receptionist continued with her praise, "Don't be so humble! After all,you're a Westfield Art Institute graduae! We're honored to have you with your international expertise return to invest in our domestic research!"

Judith blushed at the compliments.

Ella listened to their animated back-and-forth as she entered the elevator,watching the doors slowly close.

The consequences of abandoning everything for love had manifested thoroughly in her life.

What she had once rejected was now a coveted opportunity for others.

She couldn't blame anyone for looking down on her. She had brought this upon herself.

There was no point in regret. She still dared to start over. Returning to square one wasn't such a big deal.

The elevator doors opened, and Ella looked up to see Austin's good friend.

Paul Hernandez.

Ella had intended to ignore him and walk past.

"Ella!" Paul's eyes held contempt and disdain as he looked her up and
down, blocking her path. "Here for an interview? Got kicked out by Austin?



After marriage, Ella had barely left home, focusing all her attention on Austin.

She didn't answer, which only fueled his arrogance. "Cat got your tongue?With your qualifications, there's no way you'll pass this interview."

Just then, someone passing by uttered coldly, "She won't make it through;the R&D department of Quantum Tech might as well shut down." Then,turning to Ella, he commanded, "Follow me."

Raising her eyes, Ella recognized the face: Jason Carter.

Their gazes met briefly before Austin looked away dispassionately.

Ella pressed her lips together, accustomed to his indifference.
Her attention shifted to Judith momentarily, noticing her wearing the limited-edition blazer she had been searching for all morning.

So that was why she couldn't find it.

Austin had given it to Judith.

Was it to help her make a good impression at the company?

What special treatment-enough to make anyone envious!

With a bitter smile and conflicted emotions, she turned toward the familiar face and nodded. "Mr. Castillo."

Royce paused, then recognition dawned. "Ella?"

When he spoke her name, Ella had thought Royce might have forgotten her entirely.

The fact that she, at such a young age, had once turned down the renowned Royce was quite a courageous act.

It would make for an incredible anecdote in business circles.

"Yes, it's me," She confirmed.

Judith spoke first, her voice filled with mock surprise. "Ella, didn't you fail your interview? Why are you hanging around Quantum Tech? Even if you want Mr. Castillo to give you a chance, you shouldn't compromise your dignity. Dressed so provocatively-you're not planning something inappropriate with Mr. Castillo, are you?"

In just a few sentences, Judith had painted Ella as a manipulative woman willing to sleep with Royce for a job opportunity.
With her silver tongue, Judith could easily twist truth into lies.

"Women who use their bodies to get ahead don't deserve to work at Quantum Tech." Austin said coldly, his intimidating presence suggesting he believed Ella was trying to seduce Royce.


Royce understood why Austin was targeting Ella and asked, "Are you here for a job?"


"No, I'm a secretary here," Ella replied, straightening her attire and offering her professional smile.

Royce paused, finding it difficult to imagine "Phoenix" working as his secretary.

What a waste of talent!

Beside her, Austin remained cold as he stated, "Even a secretarial position is beyond her qualifications. I don't do favors for anyone."

The statement made Royce's eye twitch as he looked at Judith.

Then who was this woman?

Austin's blatant double standard was obvious to anyone with eyes.

Ella wasn't stupid-she could see that Austin had brought Judith
specifically to introduce her to Royce, even exempting her from the interview process for direct employment.

Yet when it came to Ella, he claimed to be strictly professional.

Seeing his lack of reaction and hearing his cutting words that wounded Ella. Judith smiled with satisfaction, though she still pretended to comfort him. "Austin, don't be so harsh."


His cold, emotionless eyes showed no reaction as he glanced impatiently at Royce, apparently tired of being in the same space as Ella. "Shall we continue inside?"


He clearly didn't want to remain under the same roof as Ella any longer.

Ella heard the subtext in his words.

Austin now didn't even pretend. He openly displayed his intimacy with Judith, as if wanting the whole world to see how much he loved her.

He even brought Judith, a company newcomer, to meet Royce personally.

Everyone knew he intended to establish Judith's authority and secure her position in the company.
###Chapter 23 Spilled Coffee

She pulled her lips into a frigid smile, her heart completely chilled by Austin's constant unfair treatment.

Was she already considering herself the Raymond Group's first lady?

Austin was, after all, CEO of Raymond Group.

A knock interrupted their conversation.

"Come in," Royce called.

Ella entered carrying the three coffees.

She placed the two iced Americanos in front of Austin and Royce,respectively.

To distinguish between them, Ella had mentally noted their positions.

Only the cappuccino remained.

Turning the tables.

The hot coffee cascaded over Judith's thighs, causing her to jump up with
a shrill scream.

Realizing her inappropriate outburst, Judith quickly turned a pleading look toward Austin. "Austin, it hurts so much."

"Don't be ridiculous," Austin rose quickly, draping his jacket over her shoulders and tenderly finding tissues to help her dry off.

His cold voice questioned Royce, "Is this how you select your staff,Mr.Castillo?"


The atmosphere instantly dropped to freezing.

Royce looked uncomfortably at Ella's expressionless face.

Austin was, after all, the CEO of Raymond Group, an established businessman with extensive connections in scientific research.


His assets were spread throughout the country, and his vast international network meant he could acquire any chip or component that might stump other companies.


To put it bluntly, crossing Austin while trying to succeed in scientific research would be like climbing Mount Everest.


The difficulty would increase exponentially.

But Ella was Phoenix, a formidable force in her own right within scientific
circles.

Firing this renowned scientific heavyweight to please Austin would feel like losing a billion-dollar opportunity.

Caught between these competing interests, Royce could only compromise."
Ella,apologize to Judith."

Apologize?

Ella didn't feel she had done anything wrong.

Her eyes cooled as she stared at the floor, saying nothing.

Judith sniffled theatrically, dabbing at her tears. "It's all my fault. If Ella doesn't want me at Quantum Tech, I should just give her my position in the design department."

A masterful retreat to advance.
###Chapter 24 Double Standards

With a single statement. Judith transformed Ella's coffee spill into a personal vendetta. claiming Ella was deliberately targeting her.

She even characterized it as malicious workplace competition.

Hannah had mentioned on Ella's first day that Quantum Tech had zero tolerance for such behavior.


Judith was clearly angling to get Ella fired by Royce.

"Don't cry. I'll handle this for you," Austin said with an icy glance toward Ella.


His look felt like a deliberate power play-punishment for that night.tormenting her nerves.

After all, one word from him could get her dismissed.

This job meant everything to Ella. She had fought so hard to find it.


If she lost this position...

Would she be forced back into being the dutiful housewife?

Back to living under his control, following his every command?


No.She refused.

With that single statement. Ella subtly elevated Judith's status, implying that if Judith pursued this matter,she would only make herself look petty and unkind.

She had indeed planned to make Ella look incompetent and find an excuse to have her removed.


Who would have thought Ella wwould deliberately spill coffee on her?

The limited-edition jacket she'd taken from Ella's closet was completely ruined.


That bitch.

He wasn't blind. It was obvious Judith had no response, which meant she wasn't in the right.

Judith bit her lip, her expression uncomfortable and embarrassed.

If she asked for the security footage, the truth would be revealed.
If she didn't, it would look like she was hiding something.

Royce watched the scene unfold with inner contempt, 'Is Austin so infatuated with Judith that he'd lost all objectivity? Ella makes one mistake,and he threatens termination, but when Judith is clearly in the wrong. it suddenly becomes no big deal?'

The double standard was glaringly obvious.

"Let's just move on, then. No harm done," Royce said, offering Ella a reassuring smile.

Inwardly, Ella felt a profound sadness.

What a perfect hero-saves-damsel moment.

So this was what happened when you love someone-you lose all sense of right and wrong.

She lowered her gaze, watching as Judith's lips curved downward in displeasure while Austin comfortingly patted the back of her hand.

Even these small gestures revealed how much he cared for Judith.

This was the best offer Royce could make-a position in the company's most prestigious division.


Ella didn't immediately accept.

This was actually Ella's jacket that Judith had taken from her closet.

Fifty million dollars.
Judith had taken the entire design department out for dinner on her first day.

Quantum Tech's data archives were massive, and Hannah was helping her search for the previous generation's autonomous driving data. It was a hassle.

When you love someone, you support their career at all costs.

Better to say little and do more.

Complaining about the workload in public only created enemies without solving anything.


She would have plenty of interactions with the design department in the future.

Everyone knew Judith's position at Quantum Tech wasn't ordinary-clearly orchestrated by Raymond Group's CEO.

###Chapter 25 Harsh Realities

Getting to meet Austin, CEO of Raymond Group, and sharing a meal with him was like winning the lottery.

Even if they couldn't keep their positions at Quantum Tech, a connection with Raymond could land them a job at his company, allowing they to step out and earn an admiring glance from others during social engagements.

That was how the business world worked-built on these networks of personal relationships.

|You're working at Quantum Tech?]

Too extravagant.

Anthony."

Next door.

###Chapter 26 Breaking Point

#Quantum Tech intern sleeps with executive for promotion#

###Chapter 27 To Grow Stronger

The only way to silence them was to become stronger.

Ella's gaze hardened with determination as her steps grew more purposeful.

Though the path ahead remained shrouded in uncertainty,she walked forward without fear.


At eight o'clock, Hannah suggested she head home early.

"Ella. Why push yourself so hard? You're just an intern secretary."

Ella raised both hands in surrender. "Not at all."

Ella understood Hannah was trying to cheer her up after noticing her low spirits throughout the day.

She was no longer the decorative wife everyone underestimated.
Under the sway of her silver-tongued eloquence, she secured a face-to-face meeting.

For now, it was merely beginning. Sitting in the car, Ella pondered incessantly on how she might cultivate trust with the other party upon arriving at the Midnight Mirage, to persuade them to invest.

She then entered the Midnight Mirage and accidentally bumped into Judith and Austin as they stepped out of a luxury car.

###chapter 51 Just Business

###chapter 53 Quit

###chapter 54 Breaking Free

Passing through the reception area, Ella found no office spaces, no conference rooms-just rows of server cabinets reaching to the ceiling,humming quietly.

A young man wearing black-rimmed glasses and a checkered shirt, looking barely older than Ella, led her into an isolated laboratory separated by glass walls.


The most striking feature wasn't any high-tech equipment, but an entire wall-a blackboard covered with dense, yellowing chalk formulas.


A tall, thin man with silver hair stood with his back to her, chalk in hand,seemingly modifying one of the variables.

"Dr. Adler, Ms. Brooks has arrived," The young man announced.

mean this?"

###chapter 90 Rules of the Game

###chapter 92 Breaking the Code

###chapter 93 The Prometheus's Torch

###chapter 94 The Political Game

Ella remained silent, pulling up the internal structure of the "Cradle"folder again.

Just then, the massive screen at the center of the laboratory unexpectedly lit up once more, showing a live feed of Robert lying in intensive care.

He had oxygen tubes in his nose and was connected to a cardiac monitor.Everything seemed stable.
